The 2025 Kia Carnival achieves a Poor rating in the Side Impact category [3]. The Carnival has Forward Collision-Avoidance Assist (FCA) with enhancements on SX models and above, and Highway Driving Assist 2 (HDA 2) on SX trims and above [4].
*   **Toyota Sienna:** The Toyota Sienna is consistently praised for its fuel efficiency due to its standard hybrid powertrain [11, 13, 14]. Car and Driver gives the 2025 Toyota Sienna Hybrid a 9.5/10 rating [4]. Kelley Blue Book names the Toyota Sienna as their favorite minivan because of its family-friendly interior and standard hybrid powertrain [13]. It also has a dual 12.3-inch screen setup, fridge box and vacuum [2]. The 2025 Toyota Sienna gets the top five-star crash-test rating from the NHTSA, and the Insurance Institute for Highway Safety (IIHS) named it a Top Safety Pick [2, 9]. In IIHS testing, the rear passenger dummy's head remained a safe distance from the front seatback in the updated moderate overlap front test, but the shoulder belt moved too far upward toward the dummy's neck, and the lap belt moved from the ideal position on the pelvis onto the abdomen [3]. The Toyota Sienna has Toyota Safety Sense, which includes Pre-Collision System with Pedestrian Detection, Full-Speed Range Dynamic Radar Cruise Control, and Lane Departure Alert with Steering Assist [4].
*   **Chrysler Pacifica:** The Chrysler Pacifica was named the "Best Minivan for Families" by U.S. News & World Report for the second year in a row, based on safety, reliability, space, comfort, convenience, and connectivity [5, 7, 8]. It also offers a plug-in hybrid (PHEV) option [16, 17]. In IIHS testing, the rear passenger dummy's head remained a safe distance from the front seatback in the updated moderate overlap front test, and injury values indicate a moderate risk of injury to the head or neck and chest [3]. The Chrysler Pacifica has Automated emergency braking with pedestrian detection, Blind-spot monitoring with rear cross-traffic alert, and Adaptive cruise control and lane-departure warning standard [4].
*   **Honda Odyssey:** The Honda Odyssey is known for its practicality and strong V6 engine [2]. Car and Driver gives the 2025 Honda Odyssey an 8.5/10 rating [4]. The NHTSA gives the 2025 Odyssey an overall 5 Star rating [2, 9]. In IIHS testing, the rear passenger dummy's head approached the front seatback in the updated moderate overlap front test, and injury values indicate a moderate risk of injury to the chest and a likely risk of injury to the head or neck [3]. The Honda Odyssey has Honda Sensing standard, which includes forward collision warning, automatic emergency braking and pedestrian braking, and lane departure warning [4].

Ultimately, the best minivan for you will depend on your specific needs and preferences. Consider factors like budget, desired features, fuel efficiency, safety ratings, and reliability when making your decision.

--- Research Result 4 ---
As of June 20, 2025, here's a summary of the IIHS performance results for the 2025 Kia Carnival, Toyota Sienna, Honda Odyssey, and Chrysler Pacifica in the updated moderate overlap front test and updated side crash test, with a focus on rear-seat passenger safety:

**Key IIHS Tests and Criteria:**

*   **Updated Moderate Overlap Front Test:** This test involves a vehicle striking a barrier at 40 mph with 40% of its front width overlapping. [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) The updated version includes a second dummy, representing a small woman or 12-year-old child, in the second row behind the driver. [capitalone](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [caranddriver](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) [moparinsiders](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-4) The focus is on injuries frequently seen in rear-seat occupants. [caranddriver](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2) [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) [repairerdrivennews](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [youtube](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-6)
*   **Updated Side Impact Test:** This test uses a heavier barrier (4,200 lbs) traveling at a higher speed (37 mph) compared to the original test. [thecarcrashdetective](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-7) [youtube](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-8) [reddit](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-9)
*   **IIHS Ratings:** The IIHS uses a four-category rating system: Good, Acceptable, Marginal, and Poor. [motor1](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-10) [capitalone](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-1) [repairerdrivennews](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5) [caranddriver](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-2)
*   **Top Safety Pick Criteria:** To qualify for a 2025 Top Safety Pick, a vehicle must earn good ratings in the small overlap front and updated side tests and an acceptable rating in the updated moderate overlap front test. [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) Acceptable or good headlights must come standard across all trim levels, and the vehicle must earn an acceptable or good rating in the pedestrian front crash prevention test. [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3)
*   **Top Safety Pick+ Criteria:** To qualify for a 2025 Top Safety Pick+, a vehicle needs a good rating in the updated moderate overlap front test instead of an acceptable rating. [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-0) [carbuzz](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-11) [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-3) The other criteria are identical to those for 2025 Top Safety Pick.

**Important Considerations:**

*   **Rear Seat Still Safest for Children:** Despite the noted shortcomings, the IIHS emphasizes that the back seat remains the safest place for children under 13. [autotrader](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-14)
*   **Evolving Standards:** The IIHS regularly updates its tests to reflect evolving safety concerns and encourage manufacturers to improve vehicle safety.
*   **Variations in Results:** Note that some ratings may apply to specific build dates or trim levels due to ongoing vehicle improvements.
*   **Front vs. Rear Safety:** The IIHS has observed that front seats have become safer due to improved airbags and advanced seat belts, which are not always available in the rear. [iihs](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-12) [edmunds](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-13) [repairerdrivennews](https://vertexaisearch.cloud.google.com/id/3-5)
